01

Historical Background

Company Rule (1773–1858) → Crown Rule (1858–1947) → Independence (1947)

📰
Live CA — Chapter 1 · Historical Background
Federalism · Centre-State Relations · Colonial Legacy · Princely States · Governor Powers
Click Update Now in the top bar to fetch this week's current affairs linked to this chapter.
2–4
Prelims Qs per year (average)
35%
Questions from GOI Acts 1919 & 1935
30%
From Charter Acts + Regulating Act
25%
Firsts & Key appointments
⚡ Most repeated topics: Regulating Act 1773 (G-G of Bengal), Pitt's India Act 1784 (Double Govt), Charter Act 1833 (G-G of India), ICA 1909 (Morley-Minto, communal electorate), GOI Act 1919 (dyarchy, bicameralism), GOI Act 1935 (3 lists, provincial autonomy). Historical Background questions in Prelims often appear under Modern History section, not Polity — many aspirants miss this!
ALL PYQs — Decade-Wise (1990–2025)
📜 1985–1995 — Early Pattern (Foundation Era) ▼
PRELIMS 1991
The Regulating Act was passed in the year?
✅ 1773 — 1st step by British Govt to regulate EIC. Created G-G of Bengal (Warren Hastings) and Supreme Court at Calcutta.
PRELIMS 1992
Which Act transferred the Indian government from EIC to the British Crown?
✅ Government of India Act, 1858 — Also changed G-G of India to Viceroy of India (1st = Lord Canning). Abolished Board of Control and Court of Directors.
PRELIMS 1993
Who was the first Governor-General of India (not Bengal)?
✅ Lord William Bentick — Charter Act of 1833 made him the 1st G-G of India. Earlier holders were G-G of Bengal only.
MAINS 1990 (GS)
Describe the political significance of the Government of India Act 1919.
✅ Key: Introduction of dyarchy in provinces (transferred/reserved subjects), 1st bicameralism (Council of State + Legislative Assembly), direct elections, 3 of 6 Viceroy's council members to be Indian, Chamber of Princes 1921.
MAINS 1993
Write a note on the Government of India Act 1935 as the basis of the Indian Constitution.
✅ Key: 3 Lists (Federal 59, Provincial 54, Concurrent 36), Provincial Autonomy (operative 1937), Federal Court, RBI, all became basis of Indian constitution's structure. Ambedkar: "No apologies for borrowing from 1935 Act."
PRELIMS 1994
The system of communal electorate in India was introduced by which Act?
✅ Indian Councils Act, 1909 (Morley-Minto Reforms) — Separate electorate for Muslims. Lord Minto = "Father of Communal Electorate."
PRELIMS 1995
Dyarchy was introduced in the provinces by the?
✅ Government of India Act, 1919 — Divided provincial subjects into Transferred (with responsible ministers) and Reserved (with Governor). First experiment with responsible government in India.
📗 1996–2005 — Consolidation Era ▼
PRELIMS 1996
The Indian Independence Act was passed by the British Parliament in?
✅ 1947 (introduced 4 July, Royal Assent 18 July, came into force 15 August 1947). Created two dominions: India and Pakistan.
PRELIMS 1998
The Cabinet Mission to India was headed by?
✅ Lord Pethick-Lawrence (Secretary of State for India) — assisted by Sir Stafford Cripps and A.V. Alexander. Their plan led to formation of Constituent Assembly in 1946.
PRELIMS 1999
Who introduced the Pitt's India Act in the British Parliament?
✅ William Pitt (then Prime Minister of Britain) — hence named Pitt's India Act 1784. Created Board of Control (political affairs) alongside Court of Directors (commercial affairs) = Double Government.
PRELIMS 2000
By which Act was the post of Secretary of State for India created?
✅ Government of India Act, 1858 — Secretary of State (member of British Cabinet) + 15-member Council of India. Abolished by Indian Independence Act 1947 (replaced by Secretary of State for Commonwealth Affairs).
PRELIMS 2001
The Indian Councils Act of 1861 is significant in the constitutional history of India because it?
✅ (a) Restored the legislative powers to Bombay and Madras Presidencies — reversed centralising tendency of Charter Act 1833. Also nominated Indians to Viceroy's expanded council — beginning of representative institutions.
MAINS 2001 (GS)
What was the Poona Pact of 1932? What were its major provisions?
✅ Key: Communal Award (Aug 1932) by Ramsay MacDonald gave Depressed Classes separate electorates. Gandhi fasted in protest. Poona Pact (24 Sept 1932) between Gandhi + Ambedkar: dropped separate electorate but reserved MORE seats (148 instead of 71) for Depressed Classes within Hindu joint electorate.
PRELIMS 2003
Morley-Minto Reforms is associated with which Act?
✅ Indian Councils Act, 1909 — Lord Morley = Secretary of State; Lord Minto = Viceroy. Introduced communal representation for Muslims (separate electorate), increased size of legislative councils, allowed supplementary questions.
PRELIMS 2004
Which of the following Acts introduced for the first time direct election in India?
✅ Government of India Act, 1919 — introduced direct elections alongside bicameralism (Council of State + Legislative Assembly). ICA 1892 had only indirect/limited "nomination on recommendation."
MAINS 2004 (GS)
Trace the constitutional development in India between 1858 and 1947.
✅ Model: GOI 1858 (Crown rule, Viceroy) → ICA 1861 (rep. institutions, decentralisation) → ICA 1892 (budget, questions) → ICA 1909 (Morley-Minto, communal electorate) → GOI 1919 (dyarchy, bicameralism) → GOI 1935 (provincial autonomy, 3 lists) → Independence Act 1947.
📘 2006–2015 — Analytical Era (Statement-Based Qs emerge) ▼
PRELIMS 2009
Consider the following statements about the Charter Act of 1813: 1. It ended the trade monopoly of EIC. 2. It asserted sovereignty of British Crown over Company's territories. 3. It allowed Christian missionaries to come to India. Which are correct?
✅ All three (1, 2 and 3) — BUT note: trade monopoly abolished EXCEPT for tea and trade with China (that remained until Charter Act of 1833 or later). Classic multi-statement prelims format.
PRELIMS 2010
The "portfolio system" for the management of Government business was introduced by?
✅ Lord Canning in 1859. Formally recognised by Indian Councils Act 1861. Each member of Viceroy's council made in-charge of one or more departments — direct precursor to modern Cabinet system.
PRELIMS 2012
In the context of Indian history, the Principle of Dyarchy refers to?
✅ Division of legislative subjects into Central and Provincial, and Provincial subjects into Reserved and Transferred — GOI Act 1919. Transferred: responsible to legislature (education, health, agriculture). Reserved: with Governor (police, justice, land revenue).
PRELIMS 2014
The demand for Constituent Assembly was made in 1934 by?
✅ M.N. Roy — pioneer of communist movement in India. 1935 = INC officially demanded it. 1938 = Nehru declared it must be on adult franchise. 1940 = August Offer accepted in principle.
PRELIMS 2015
The Government of India Act 1919 clearly defined: The separation of power between judiciary and legislature / The jurisdiction of central and provincial governments / The powers and functions of the Secretary of State?
✅ (b) The jurisdiction of central and provincial governments — through "Devolution Rules" which divided subjects into Central and Provincial. The Act established dyarchy in provinces — NOT separation of judiciary/legislature (that was 1853 act).
MAINS 2015 (GS-II)
It would have been difficult for the Constituent Assembly to complete its historic task of drafting the Constitution in just three years but for the experience gained with the Government of India Act, 1935. Discuss.
✅ Classic Mains question — reappears almost every 5 years. Key points: (1) Federal scheme directly from 1935 Act (2) Emergency provisions model (3) Judiciary structure (4) Governors (5) Public Service Commissions (6) Over half the provisions traceable to 1935. Ambedkar: "No apologies for borrowing — details of administration need not be innovative."
📙 2016–2020 — Critical Thinking Era ▼
MAINS 2016 (GS-II)
Did the Government of India Act 1935 lay down a federal constitution? Discuss.
✅ Federal features: 3 lists, bicameralism in 6 provinces, Federal Court, Governor-General. BUT: Federation never formed (princes refused), dyarchy at Centre never operative, residuary powers with Viceroy (not Centre or Provinces), All-India services = unitary. Conclusion: quasi-federal in design, never truly federal in practice. K.C. Wheare on Indian constitution = "quasi-federal" = continued tradition from 1935 Act.
PRELIMS 2017
Who among the following first propounded the idea of Constituent Assembly to frame a constitution for India?
✅ M.N. Roy — in 1934. Swaraj Party (1924) also raised it but M.N. Roy is specifically credited with first formally propounding the idea. INC officially endorsed in 1935.
PRELIMS 2019
With reference to the Government of India Act 1919, which of the following is/are correct? 1. It provided for the establishment of a central legislature with two chambers. 2. It extended franchise to a limited number of people.
✅ Both correct (1 and 2) — 1919 Act introduced bicameralism (Council of State + Legislative Assembly) = 1st time. Also granted franchise to limited people based on property/tax qualifications — about 2-3% of population initially.
PRELIMS 2019
Which Act introduced Dyarchy in the Provinces of British India?
✅ Government of India Act, 1919 — direct, factual question that repeats every few years. Always distinguish: Dyarchy in PROVINCES = 1919. Dyarchy AT CENTRE (proposed, never operative) = 1935 Act.
MAINS 2019 (GS-II)
Whether the Indian federation is a true federation. Comment. (250 words)
✅ Key: India ≠ true federation. Use 1935 Act lineage: residuary powers with Viceroy (Centre today), strong Centre features (Art 1 "Union of States" not Federation, Governor appointment, all-India services, Art 3 unilateral boundary change, Emergency provisions). Quote: K.C. Wheare (quasi-federal), Granville Austin (co-operative federalism). Conclude: India = cooperative federalism with centralising tendency — pragmatic federal design suited to post-partition reality.
📔 2021–2025 — Statement/Assertion Era (Highest Difficulty) ▼
PRELIMS 2021
Consider the statements: 1. The first Governor-General of India was appointed under the Government of India Act 1858. 2. Under the Government of India Act 1858, the British Parliament exercised direct control over the Governor-General.
✅ Statement 1: FALSE — 1st Viceroy/G-G under 1858 Act = Lord Canning. But G-G of India (not Viceroy) was created under Charter Act 1833 (Bentick). Statement 2: FALSE — British Parliament controlled via Secretary of State, not directly. Classic trap: confusing G-G of Bengal (1773) vs G-G of India (1833) vs Viceroy (1858).
PRELIMS 2022
With reference to the history of India, "Dyarchy" refers to which of the following? (a) Division of Indian Empire in two parts — provinces and princely states (b) Introduction of double government in India by having two sets of civil servants (c) Having two houses of the Central Legislature (d) Division of legislative subjects into two categories, Central and Provincial, and Provincial into Reserved and Transferred
✅ (d) — Division of provincial subjects into Reserved (with Governor) and Transferred (with Ministers responsible to legislature). Under GOI Act 1919. Classic definitional trap with option (c) trying to confuse with bicameralism.
PRELIMS 2023
By which Act was the Governor General of Bengal designated as Governor General of India?
✅ Charter Act of 1833 — Lord William Bentick = 1st G-G of India. The Act also deprived Bombay and Madras Governors of legislative powers, ended EIC's commercial role, and is called "final step of centralisation."
PRELIMS 2024
Consider following statements about ICA 1861: 1. It made a beginning of representative institutions by associating Indians with law-making. 2. It initiated decentralisation by restoring legislative powers to Bombay and Madras. 3. It laid foundation of bicameralism in India.
✅ Statements 1 and 2 correct. Statement 3 WRONG — bicameralism was introduced by GOI Act 1919 (not 1861). 1861 reversed the centralising trend but didn't introduce bicameralism. Trap for unprepared candidates.
PRELIMS 2025
Consider statements about GOI Act 1935: 1. It provided for the establishment of a Federal Court. 2. Residuary powers were given to the Central legislature. 3. It separated Burma from India.
✅ Statement 1 CORRECT (Federal Court set up 1937). Statement 2 WRONG — residuary powers given to Viceroy/Governor-General, not central legislature. Statement 3 CORRECT (Burma separated under 1935 Act). Answer: 1 and 3 only. Residuary powers trap is extremely common in Prelims.
KEY ACTS — Quick Reference
1773 PRE ⭐⭐⭐ · 4+ times asked
Regulating Act — Foundation of Central Administration
  • 1st step to control & regulate EIC — recognised political & admin functions
  • Governor of Bengal → Governor-General of Bengal (1st = Warren Hastings)
  • Bombay & Madras subordinated to Bengal G-G
  • Supreme Court at Calcutta (1774): 1 CJ + 3 judges
1784 PRE ⭐⭐⭐ · 3+ times asked
Pitt's India Act — Double Government
  • Separated commercial vs political functions of EIC
  • Created Board of Control for political affairs → Double Government
  • EIC territories first called "British Possessions in India"
1833 PRE ⭐⭐⭐ · Asked 2023
Charter Act 1833 — Final Centralisation
  • G-G of Bengal → G-G of India (1st = Lord William Bentick)
  • Bombay & Madras lost legislative powers
  • EIC became purely administrative; Laws now called "Acts" (earlier: "Regulations")
1853 PRE ⭐⭐
Charter Act 1853 — Last Charter Act
  • 1st separation of legislative & executive functions → Indian Legislative Council
  • Open competition for civil servants (Macaulay Committee 1854)
  • 1st local representation in Central Legislature (4 provincial members)
1858 PRE ⭐⭐⭐ · 5+ times asked
GOI Act 1858 — After 1857 Revolt
  • Transferred power to British Crown; G-G of India → Viceroy (1st = Lord Canning)
  • Ended Double Government (Board of Control + Court of Directors abolished)
  • Secretary of State for India created (15-member Council of India)
1861 PRE ⭐⭐ · Asked 2024
Indian Councils Act 1861 — Representative Institutions Begin
  • 1st Indians nominated to Viceroy's council (Raja of Benaras, Maharaja of Patiala, Sir Dinkar Rao)
  • Restored legislative powers to Bombay & Madras (decentralisation)
  • Recognised portfolio system (Canning 1859); Viceroy can issue ordinances (6 months)
1909 PRE ⭐⭐⭐ · 5+ times asked
ICA 1909 — Morley-Minto Reforms (Communal Electorate)
  • Central council: 16 → 60 members
  • 1st Indian in Viceroy's Executive Council: Satyendra Prasad Sinha (Law Member)
  • Separate Electorate for Muslims — Lord Minto = "Father of Communal Electorate"
1919 PRE ⭐⭐⭐ · 6+ times asked MAINS ⭐⭐
GOI Act 1919 — Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms
  • British declared "Gradual responsible Government" (20 Aug 1917)
  • DYARCHY in provinces: Transferred (education, health, agri — ministers responsible) vs Reserved (police, justice, land revenue — Governor alone)
  • 1st bicameralism + direct elections (Council of State + Legislative Assembly)
  • Chamber of Princes (Narendra Mandal) 1921; CPSC 1926
1935 PRE ⭐⭐⭐ · Most asked act MAINS ⭐⭐⭐
GOI Act 1935 — 321 Sections, 10 Schedules (Longest Act)
  • All-India Federation — never formed (princes refused)
  • Three Lists: Federal (59), Provincial (54), Concurrent (36); Residuary with Viceroy (⚠️ TRAP: NOT with Centre or states)
  • Abolished dyarchy in provinces → Provincial Autonomy (operative 1937, ended 1939)
  • Dyarchy at Centre — proposed but never operative
  • RBI, Federal Court (1937), separated Burma, created Orissa & Sind
1947 PRE ⭐⭐
Indian Independence Act 1947
  • Independence: 15 Aug 1947. Mountbatten Plan (3 Jun 1947) → partition
  • 1st G-G of India = Mountbatten; 1st PM = Nehru. Dropped "Emperor of India" title.
  • Lapse of British paramountcy over princely states; CA became Parliament of Indian Dominion

📰 Current Affairs 2024–25 Linked to Chapter 1
2025 · FEDERALISM REFORM
Kurian Joseph Committee (Tamil Nadu) — Federal Reforms 2025
High-Level Committee recommended structural reset of Indian federalism — arguing excessive centralisation traces directly to colonial-era Acts (GOI 1919 Devolution Rules, GOI 1935 residuary powers with Viceroy). Proposes amending Art 368 to require state ratification, moving Education back to State List, revising GST Council voting. Static link: The "unitary bias" in Indian federalism directly continues the 1935 Act's design.
→ Mains: "Suggest measures to strengthen federalism" — cite this committee
NOV 2024 · INTEGRATION OF PRINCELY STATES
J&K Celebrates Constitution Day for First Time (26 Nov 2024)
Following Art 370 abrogation (2019) and bifurcation (J&K + Ladakh as UTs), J&K celebrated Constitution Day 2024 for first time in 74 years. Static link: Indian Independence Act 1947 — lapse of paramountcy → Instrument of Accession (Oct 1947) → special status under Art 370 → its removal in 2019 completes the integration that started with independence.
→ Prelims: Art 370, UT; Mains: federalism, integration of princely states
🧠 30-Year Pattern — What NEVER Gets Asked
Charter Act 1793 & Act of 1786 = almost NEVER in Prelims
These Acts (1786, 1793) have appeared fewer than 2 times each in 30 years. Don't waste time memorising their details. Focus on: Regulating 1773 · Pitt's 1784 · Charter 1833 · Charter 1853 · GOI 1858 · ICA 1861 · ICA 1909 · GOI 1919 · GOI 1935 · Indep 1947 — these 10 accounts for 95%+ of questions.
02

Making of the Constitution

Demand (1934) → Cabinet Mission (1946) → Adopted (26 Nov 1949) → Enforced (26 Jan 1950)

📰
Live CA — Chapter 2 · Making of Constitution
Basic Structure · Amendment Power · Preamble Debates · Constituent Assembly Legacy
Click Update Now in the top bar to fetch this week's current affairs linked to this chapter.
📊 30-Year Exam Pattern — Chapter 2
2–3
Prelims Qs per year (average)
40%
Questions on key dates & persons
35%
Drafting Committee & Committees
25%
CA criticism & Objectives Resolution
⚡ Most-tested: Dates (9 Dec 1946, 13 Dec 1946, 29 Aug 1947, 26 Nov 1949, 26 Jan 1950), Sachchidananda Sinha (provisional chairman), Drafting Committee members (especially replacements), Objectives Resolution (Nehru moved, not Patel/Gandhi), "26 Nov = Constitution Day (not enforcement day)."
Post-2020: Statement-based traps on exact dates and persons are the dominant format.
ALL PYQs — Decade-Wise (1990–2025)
📜 1985–1995 — Foundation Era ▼
PRELIMS 1989
Who was the Chairman of the Constituent Assembly of India?
✅ Dr. Rajendra Prasad — elected permanent Chairman on 11 Dec 1946. Earlier, Dr. Sachchidananda Sinha was temporary/provisional chairman on 9 Dec 1946. Common trap: confuse the two.
PRELIMS 1990
Who was the first person to put forward the idea of Constituent Assembly for India?
✅ M.N. Roy — in 1934. Pioneer of communist movement in India. INC officially endorsed in 1935. Many confuse with Nehru's 1938 demand or the Cabinet Mission 1946.
MAINS 1991
Write a short note: The Objectives Resolution of the Constituent Assembly.
✅ Key: Moved by Nehru on 13 Dec 1946, adopted unanimously 22 Jan 1947. 8 key commitments: sovereign independent republic, union of territories, autonomous units with residuary powers, power from people, justice/equality/freedom, safeguards for minorities, territorial integrity, world peace. Modified version = Preamble of Constitution.
PRELIMS 1993
The Constituent Assembly of India was set up under which plan?
✅ Cabinet Mission Plan of 1946 — headed by Lord Pethick-Lawrence. Rejected idea of two CAs (Muslim League's demand), created one CA of 389 members (296 British India + 93 Princely States).
PRELIMS 1994
How many members signed the Constitution of India on 26 November 1949?
✅ 284 members — out of total 299. CA met for 11 sessions over 2 years, 11 months, 18 days. Constitution had 395 articles, 8 schedules and a Preamble on adoption.
PRELIMS 1995
Why was 26th January chosen as the date for the enforcement of the Constitution?
✅ Historical significance: 26 January 1930 = Purna Swaraj Day — following Lahore Session (Dec 1929) of INC. This was the date when Indian National Congress first celebrated Independence Day. Hence chosen to honour this historical commitment to complete independence.
📗 1996–2005 ▼
PRELIMS 1997
When was the Constituent Assembly set up?
✅ November 1946 under Cabinet Mission Plan. First meeting: 9 Dec 1946. Muslim League boycotted first meeting. Princely States initially stayed away — joined later in 1947.
PRELIMS 1999
Who was the legal advisor/constitutional advisor to the Constituent Assembly?
✅ Sir B.N. Rau — appointed as constitutional advisor (legal advisor). Also served as India's representative to UN. Key person: different from S.N. Mukherjee (Chief Draftsman) and Ambedkar (Chairman, Drafting Committee).
PRELIMS 2001
The Constitution of India came into force on 26th January 1950. Before this date, which Act governed India?
✅ Government of India Act, 1935 — with modifications as provided under Indian Independence Act 1947. The CA itself drafted laws under its legislative capacity as Parliament of Dominion India.
PRELIMS 2003
Who among the following was the Chairman of the Drafting Committee of the Indian Constitution?
✅ Dr. B.R. Ambedkar — Chairman of Drafting Committee (set up 29 Aug 1947). Also known as "Father of Constitution" and "Chief Architect of Constitution." Piloted the draft through the CA.
PRELIMS 2004
How many amendments were proposed to the Draft Constitution during its consideration?
✅ 7,653 amendments proposed — 2,473 actually discussed and disposed of. Total 114 days spent on draft constitution. CA met for 11 sessions over 2 years, 11 months and 18 days. Cost = ₹64 lakh.
📘 2006–2015 ▼
PRELIMS 2009
Consider following about Constituent Assembly: 1. Composition based on scheme of Cabinet Mission 1946. 2. Central Legislature of India served as the Constituent Assembly from 1946 until first general elections. 3. Members of CA elected on the basis of adult franchise.
✅ Statement 1 CORRECT. Statement 2 WRONG — CA became a legislative body (Dominion Parliament) but was not the Central Legislature of pre-Independence India. Statement 3 WRONG — Members were indirectly elected by provincial assemblies (limited franchise, not adult franchise). Answer: Only 1 correct.
PRELIMS 2013
Consider following statements: 1. The CA was not based on universal adult franchise. 2. Elections to CA were held in July-August 1946.
✅ Both CORRECT — indirectly elected by provincial assemblies (which themselves were on limited franchise). Elections held July-August 1946. Congress won 208 of 296 seats.
PRELIMS 2014
Who among the following was calligrapher of the Constitution of India?
✅ Prem Behari Narain Raizada — calligraphed the English version in a flowing italic style. Hindi version calligraphy by Vasant Krishan Vaidya. Beautification by Nand Lal Bose and Beohar Rammanohar Sinha (Shantiniketan).
MAINS 2015 (GS-II)
It would have been difficult for the CA to complete its task without experience from GOI Act 1935. Discuss.
✅ Repeated from 2015 — likely to come again in 2026! Key: 1935 Act gave structural skeleton. Federal scheme, emergency powers, judiciary model, Governors, UPSC, administrative details — all from 1935. Ambedkar's famous defence: "No apologies for borrowing."
📙 2016–2020 ▼
MAINS 2016 (GS-II)
Discuss each adjective attached to the word 'Republic' in the Preamble. Are they defendable in the present circumstances?
✅ Republic adjectives: Sovereign, Socialist, Secular, Democratic. Sovereign: India not subject to external authority — YES (but WTO, IMF raise questions). Socialist: welfare state, mixed economy — YES (Balram Singh 2024 upheld). Secular: equal respect to all religions — contested but SC says YES basic structure. Democratic: elections, universal franchise — YES but declining institutions concern exists.
PRELIMS 2018
Consider: 1. Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel moved the Objectives Resolution in the CA. 2. The majority of Constitution came into force on 26 Nov 1949.
✅ Both WRONG. Statement 1: Objectives Resolution moved by Nehru (not Patel) on 13 Dec 1946. Statement 2: Majority came into force on 26 Jan 1950; only some provisions (citizenship, elections etc.) came into force on 26 Nov 1949. Classic double trap!
PRELIMS 2019
With reference to the Objectives Resolution, which of the following is not correct? (a) It envisioned an independent India. (b) It was moved by Nehru. (c) It was adopted on 26 Jan 1947. (d) It laid down fundamentals of constitutional structure.
✅ (c) is INCORRECT — Objectives Resolution was adopted on 22 January 1947, not 26 January. Moved on 13 Dec 1946, adopted 22 Jan 1947. This confusion with Republic Day date is a perennial trap.
📔 2021–2025 — Trap-Heavy Era ▼
PRELIMS 2021
Who was the Chairman of the Union Constitution Committee of the Constituent Assembly?
✅ Jawaharlal Nehru — NOT Ambedkar (common trap). Ambedkar chaired the Drafting Committee. Nehru chaired: Union Powers Committee + Union Constitution Committee + States Committee. Patel chaired: Provincial Constitution Committee + Advisory Committee (FR, Minorities, Tribal Areas).
PRELIMS 2023 ⚠️
Statement I: Constitution Day is celebrated on 26 Nov to promote constitutional values. Statement II: On 26 Nov 1949, the CA set up the Drafting Committee under Ambedkar to prepare the Draft Constitution.
✅ Statement I: CORRECT. Statement II: DELIBERATELY FALSE — Drafting Committee was set up on 29 Aug 1947, NOT 26 Nov 1949. On 26 Nov 1949, the Constitution was adopted and signed. This is the most-discussed UPSC trap of recent years. Answer: (c) S-I correct, S-II incorrect.
PRELIMS 2024
Who was the Provisional/Temporary Chairman of the CA on its first meeting on 9 December 1946?
✅ Dr. Sachchidananda Sinha — oldest member, elected following French practice. Dr. Rajendra Prasad became permanent President on 11 Dec 1946. Distinguish: Sachchidananda Sinha (temporary) ≠ Rajendra Prasad (permanent).
MAINS 2025 (GS-II)
The Indian Constitution has conferred the amending power on the ordinary legislative institutions with a few procedural hurdles. Examine the procedural and substantive limitations on the amending power of Parliament. (250w)
✅ Procedural: Art 368 types (special majority; special majority + state ratification; simple majority outside Art 368). Substantive: Basic Structure doctrine (Kesavananda 1973) — Parliament cannot destroy core identity. Elements of basic structure: federalism, secularism, democracy, judicial review, rule of law (Balram Singh 2024 reaffirmed). Conclude: India's amendment process = constrained sovereignty.
KEY DATES — 30-Year High-Frequency Table
DateEventExam Alert

11 Dec 1946Dr. Rajendra Prasad elected permanent PresidentDistinguishes from 9 Dec

22 Jan 1947Objectives Resolution adopted unanimouslyNOT 26 Jan — trap 2019!

24 Jan 1950National Anthem + Song adopted; Rajendra Prasad = 1st PresidentTwo days before Republic Day

⚠️
BIGGEST TRAP of last 10 years: "Drafting Committee was set up on 29 Aug 1947." If a statement says it was on 26 Nov 1949 — it is WRONG. Constitution was adopted on 26 Nov 1949, Drafting Committee formed two years earlier.

📰 Current Affairs 2024–25 Linked to Chapter 2
26 NOV 2024 · 75 YEARS OF CONSTITUTION
Balram Singh v. UOI (2024) — "Socialist" & "Secular" are Basic Structure
SC dismissed challenges to "socialist" and "secular" in Preamble (42nd Amendment 1976). Key: These terms are integral to Basic Structure; Constitution is a living document. Historical irony: CA itself REJECTED inserting "secular" and "socialist" in 1948 (Prof. K.T. Shah's proposals). Yet 42nd Amendment added them — SC 2024 upheld this as valid exercise of Art 368.
→ Mains model: "Debate on 'socialist' and 'secular' in Preamble" — use CA history + Balram Singh 2024
2024–25 · BASIC STRUCTURE CONTINUOUSLY IN NEWS
ONOE Bill + Waqf Amendment + Delimitation — All Invoke Basic Structure
ONOE (129th Amendment Bill 2024) — does it violate federalism as basic structure? Waqf Amendment Act 2024 — does it violate secularism and minority rights as basic structure? Delimitation freeze — representation as basic structure? All rooted in Kesavananda Bharati 1973 — Parliament's Art 368 power cannot alter basic structure.
→ Mains 2026: "Parliament's amending power and its substantive limits" — connect Ch 2 (CA), Ch 4 (Amendment procedure, Basic Structure)
03

Concept of the Constitution

Meaning → Functions → Qualities → Classification → Constitutionalism

📰
Live CA — Chapter 3 · Concept of Constitution
Constitutionalism · Preamble · Living Document · Basic Structure · Rigid vs Flexible
Click Update Now in the top bar to fetch this week's current affairs linked to this chapter.
📊 30-Year Exam Pattern — Chapter 3
1–2
Prelims Qs per year
50%
Questions on "Constitutional Govt = Limited Govt"
30%
Classification & examples (rigid/flexible, federal/unitary)
20%
Preamble legal status
⚡ 30-year pattern: "Constitutional government = limited government" is asked nearly every 3-4 years. Prelims format: 4 options where only (d) limited government is correct. Mains uses Ch 3 to compare India with UK/USA/France. "Rigid vs flexible" examples come up 2+ times per decade.
ALL PYQs — Decade-Wise (1988–2025)
📜 1988–1995 ▼
MAINS 1988
Discuss the concept of "Constitutional Government."
✅ Key: Constitutional Government = Limited Government (Roucek, Wheare). Based on rule of law, not arbitrary power. Features: separation of powers, judicial review, fundamental rights, free elections. India fulfils all — written constitution, independent judiciary, FRs, democratic elections. Contrast with authoritarian states that have constitutions but not constitutionalism.
MAINS 1991
Discuss the nature of the Indian Constitution — is it federal or unitary?
✅ Key: India = quasi-federal (K.C. Wheare). Has BOTH federal features (2 govts, 3 lists, SC, bicameralism) AND unitary features (strong centre, single citizenship, single constitution, Governor appointment, emergency provisions). Art 1 = "Union of States" not Federation. K.C. Wheare's definition helps: India doesn't fit purely federal/unitary, hence quasi-federal.
PRELIMS 1992
The Constitution of India is?
(a) Rigid (b) Flexible (c) Neither rigid nor flexible (d) Both rigid and flexible
✅ (c) Neither rigid nor flexible — India's Constitution is a synthesis of both. Some parts can be amended by simple majority (like ordinary law = flexible). Some by special majority only. Some by special majority + ratification by half states (rigid). Lord Bryce's classification = rigid or flexible. India = blend of both.
PRELIMS 1995
A Constitutional Government by definition is a government with?
(a) Written Constitution (b) Popular elections (c) Separation of powers (d) Limited powers
✅ (d) Limited powers — This is the DEFINITIONAL answer. Roucek: "Constitutionalism = limited government." A country can have written constitution WITHOUT constitutionalism (dictatorship). This question has appeared in variants 5+ times in 30 years.
📗 1996–2005 ▼
PRELIMS 1999
The British Constitution is: (a) Written and rigid (b) Unwritten and flexible (c) Written and flexible (d) Unwritten and rigid
✅ (b) Unwritten and flexible — UK Constitution = uncodified (not in one document), exists in conventions, charters, statutes. Can be amended by simple majority of Parliament (flexible). Classic classification question that comes almost every decade.
MAINS 2002
What is the difference between a written and unwritten constitution? Give examples.
✅ Written/Codified: USA, Canada, Japan, France, India — deliberate creation, in a document, enacted constitution. Unwritten/Uncodified: UK, New Zealand, Israel — evolved over time, in conventions/charters/judicial decisions/statutes, cumulative constitution. Note: "Unwritten" doesn't mean nothing is written — just not in ONE document.
PRELIMS 2003
Which of the following countries has a Federal form of Government?
(a) China (b) Cuba (c) Australia (d) Belgium
✅ (c) Australia — Federal. China = Unitary. Cuba = Unitary. Belgium is also federal but Australia is the standard UPSC example. Federal countries: USA, Switzerland, Australia, Canada, Russia, Brazil, India (quasi), Germany.
MAINS 2004
Discuss the relationship between Constitution and Constitutionalism.
✅ Key difference: A country can have a constitution but NOT constitutionalism. Constitutionalism = limited government, rule of law, not arbitrary power. A constitution is a document; constitutionalism is a philosophy. Henkin's 8 elements (popular sovereignty, rule of law, separation of powers, independent judiciary, civilian control of military, etc.) Louis Henkin. India has both — written constitution + constitutionalism through SC's Basic Structure doctrine.
📘 2006–2015 ▼
PRELIMS 2010
Consider: 1. USA has unwritten constitution. 2. UK has a written constitution. 3. India has neither rigid nor flexible constitution.
✅ Statement 1: WRONG — USA has WRITTEN constitution (1787). Statement 2: WRONG — UK has UNWRITTEN constitution. Statement 3: CORRECT — India is a synthesis. Answer: Only 3 is correct. This variant of the classification question appears every 3-4 years.
PRELIMS 2015
A constitutional government by definition is a: (a) government by legislature (b) popular government (c) multi-party government (d) limited government
✅ (d) limited government — Roucek's definition. This EXACT question reappeared again in 2015 after being asked in 1995! Definitional questions on constitutionalism recur every decade in Prelims.
📙 2016–2025 — Modern Era ▼
PRELIMS 2020
The Preamble to the Constitution of India is: (a) Not a part of Constitution, no legal effect (b) Part of Constitution, has no legal effect independently of other parts (c) Part of Constitution with same legal effect as any other part (d) Not a part of Constitution but guides interpretation
✅ (b) Part of Constitution but has no legal effect independently of other parts — Preamble is part of Constitution (Kesavananda 1973; LIC of India 1995). But it cannot be independently enforced in court — it guides interpretation of other provisions. This exact question asked 3 times in different years.
PRELIMS 2021
A Constitutional Government is one which: 1. Places effective restrictions on individual liberty in interest of State Authority. 2. Places effective restrictions on Authority of State in interest of individual liberty.
✅ Statement 2 only — Constitutional Govt = limits the STATE (not individual liberty). This is a conceptual trap: students confuse "constitutional govt limits individuals" vs "constitutional govt limits the state." The whole point of constitutionalism is to RESTRAIN state power.
PRELIMS 2023
The chief purpose of the Constitution of a country: (a) Determines objectives for making laws (b) Enables creation of political offices (c) Defines and limits the powers of government (d) Secures social justice, equality and security
✅ (c) Defines and limits the powers of government — Same conceptual answer as 1995 and 2015 but in a new format. UPSC loves this concept. Even if you forget everything else in Ch 3, remember: Constitution = defines and limits government power = Constitutionalism = Limited Government.
MAINS 2023 (GS-II)
Compare and contrast British and Indian approaches to Parliamentary Sovereignty. [10 Marks]
✅ UK: Parliament is ABSOLUTELY sovereign — no court can strike down Parliament's law. India: Parliament is CONDITIONALLY sovereign — SC can review laws (judicial review), Basic Structure limits Parliament, written Constitution is supreme. India = synthesis (Ch 4 Feature 6). Specific difference: India's "procedure established by law" (Art 21) vs UK parliamentary sovereignty with no such written limit.
MAINS 2025 (GS-II)
"Constitutional morality is the fulcrum which acts as an essential check upon high functionaries and citizens alike." Explain the concept and its application for balance between judicial independence and accountability. (250w)
✅ Constitutional morality = adherence to constitutional values (not popular morality). SC's concept from Navtej Singh Johar 2018, Puttaswamy 2017. Requires institutions to follow constitutional spirit even when politically unpopular. Link to Ch 3: Constitutionalism = limited government through internalized adherence to constitutional values, not just formal compliance.

📰 Current Affairs 2024–25 Linked to Chapter 3
2024 · CONSTITUTIONALISM IN ACTION
Balram Singh v. UOI (2024) + ONOE Bill = Constitutionalism Tested
Balram Singh 2024: SC uses core Ch 3 concepts — "Constitution is a living document" (= adaptability quality), "limited government" (= constitutionalism), Preamble as integral but not independently enforceable. ONOE Bill 2024: Critics invoke constitutionalism — a Parliament that can unilaterally override state electoral cycles violates "limited government" principle (federalism as constraint on central power).
Static link: Constitutionalism = limited government. Prescriptive constitution (India) commits to federalism, secularism — these are LIMITS on Parliament's power.
→ Mains: "Constitutionalism and parliamentary democracy" — core Ch 3 × Ch 4 hybrid question
2025 · CODIFYING BASIC STRUCTURE = MAKING IT RIGID
Kurian Joseph Committee — Proposal to Codify Basic Structure in Art 368
Proposed inserting explicit "Basic Features" clause in Art 368 — would make certain features (federalism, secularism, democracy, judicial review) completely unamendable. Static link (Ch 3): If adopted, India would move from "synthesis of rigid & flexible" (current) towards a more rigid constitution for core features. This is the prescriptive constitution principle — the state commits to certain societal goals and makes them constitutionally entrenched.
→ Prelims: Rigid/flexible classification; Mains: "Should India explicitly codify Basic Structure?"
04

Salient Features of the Constitution

17 features · Highest Mains yield · Heaviest current affairs linkage · 30 years of continuous questions

📰
Live CA — Chapter 4 · Salient Features
Federalism · Secularism · Emergency · Judicial Review · Parliamentary System · Amendments
Click Update Now in the top bar to fetch this week's current affairs linked to this chapter.
📊 30-Year Exam Pattern — Chapter 4
3–6
Prelims Qs per year (highest of all 4 chapters)
2–3
Mains GS-II Qs per year (perennial)
Every year
Federalism in Mains (30/30 years!)
Every 2yr
Secularism asked in Mains
⚡ 30-year pattern: Federalism is the single most-asked topic in Mains GS-II (appeared in some form every year since 1990). Secularism appears every 2 years. Parliamentary vs Presidential, Judicial review vs Parliamentary sovereignty, Emergency provisions (especially Art 352 "internal disturbance → armed rebellion" trap) are Prelims perennials. Sources of Constitution question appears every 3-4 years.
ALL PYQs — Decade-Wise (1985–2025)
📜 1985–1995 — Foundation Era ▼
MAINS 1986
What do you understand by "parliamentary form of government"? Compare it with the Presidential form.
✅ Parliamentary: collective responsibility, PM as real executive, can be removed by legislature, fusion of legislature + executive. Presidential (USA): separation of powers, fixed term, President directly elected, independent of legislature. India chose parliamentary because of its colonial experience with Westminster model, need for accountability, and complexity of multi-party system in diverse country.
MAINS 1988
Discuss the federal features of the Indian Constitution.
✅ Key federal features: 2 governments, 3-tier distribution of powers (7th Schedule), written constitution, supremacy of constitution, independent judiciary, bicameralism. BUT India also has strong unitary features (see Ch 4 Feature 4). Always acknowledge quasi-federal nature. Cite K.C. Wheare.
MAINS 1991
Discuss the secular nature of Indian polity and the position provided in the Constitution.
✅ India = positive secularism (equal respect to all religions). NOT negative secularism (strict church-state separation like France). Art 25-28 provide for religious freedom. State can regulate religious practices if they are social evils (e.g., untouchability). This Mains question from 1991 was asked again in variant forms in 2005, 2014, 2019, 2024 — it NEVER stops!
PRELIMS 1993
The Indian Constitution provides for the 'Judicial Review' following which country?
✅ United States of America (USA) — but India's judicial review is NARROWER because India uses "procedure established by law" (Art 21) not "due process of law" (USA). SC can review laws for procedural compliance; in USA, courts also review for substantive fairness.
PRELIMS 1994
Which of the following does not find mention in the Preamble? (a) Justice (b) Liberty (c) Fraternity (d) Federal
✅ (d) Federal — Preamble says: Sovereign, Socialist, Secular, Democratic, Republic; Justice (social, economic, political); Liberty; Equality; Fraternity. The word "Federal" does NOT appear in the Preamble or Article 1 (which says "Union of States"). This distinction is asked every few years.
MAINS 1995
The Constitution of India is described as a 'Quasi-Federal' Constitution. Explain.
✅ K.C. Wheare coined "quasi-federal" — India doesn't fit either purely federal (like USA) or purely unitary (like UK). Federal form (two governments, division of powers, SC) with unitary spirit (strong Centre, single citizenship, emergency provisions transform federal → unitary without formal amendment). This EXACT Mains question repeated in 2002, 2005, 2008, 2014, 2019, 2022!
📗 1996–2005 ▼
PRELIMS 1997
Which one of the following features of the Indian Constitution shows its federal character?
(a) Independent Judiciary (b) Fundamental Rights (c) Single citizenship (d) Directive Principles
✅ (a) Independent Judiciary — acts as arbiter between Centre and States, ensuring federal principle. Single citizenship = UNITARY feature. FRs and DPSPs apply to all = not specifically federal. This Q tests understanding of which features are federal vs unitary.
MAINS 1998
Examine the sources of the Indian Constitution. How far has India benefited from these foreign sources?
✅ Primary source: GOI Act 1935 (structure, emergency, governors, UPSC). Philosophical: USA (FRs, judicial review), Ireland (DPSP), USSR (FDs). Political: UK (parliamentary model, cabinet system). Benefit: India got proven, tested models without reinventing. Adaptation: modified for Indian conditions (positive secularism vs French laïcité, quasi-federal vs pure federal). Criticism: "borrowed constitution" — Ambedkar's defence.
MAINS 2000
Discuss the issues of federalism in India in the context of Centre-State relations.
✅ Issues: Governor appointment, Art 356 misuse (pre-SR Bommai), single party dominance, emergency provisions, all-India services, Finance Commission design. Solutions: Sarkaria Commission (1983), SR Bommai 1994 (SC restricted Art 356 misuse). This is the prototype Mains question on federalism — a variant asked EVERY year.
MAINS 2001
What are the different kinds of emergencies under the Indian Constitution? Describe each type.
✅ 3 types: (1) Art 352 — National Emergency (war/external aggression/armed rebellion — NOTE: "internal disturbance" changed to "armed rebellion" by 44th Amendment 1978). (2) Art 356/365 — State Emergency / President's Rule. (3) Art 360 — Financial Emergency (never proclaimed). Effects of each: National → FRs (except 20, 21) suspended, Parliament controls state legislation. State → State Assembly suspended. Financial → Centre controls state finances.
PRELIMS 2003
Which one of the following is NOT a feature of the parliamentary form of government?
(a) Collective responsibility (b) Judicial supremacy (c) Executive responsible to legislature (d) Membership of ministers in legislature
✅ (b) Judicial supremacy — Judicial supremacy is associated with the PRESIDENTIAL form (USA). Parliamentary form features: collective responsibility, cabinet responsible to legislature, ministers must be members of legislature, PM leads government.
MAINS 2005
How does the Indian Constitution strike a balance between Parliamentary Sovereignty and Judicial Supremacy?
✅ India = synthesis. Parliament can amend most of Constitution (parliamentary sovereignty). SC can declare laws unconstitutional through judicial review (judicial supremacy). BUT Basic Structure (Kesavananda 1973) = ultimate limit on Parliament. Art 21 uses "procedure established by law" (not USA's "due process") = India's judicial review is narrower than USA but exists unlike UK where no judicial review of Parliament's laws.
📘 2006–2015 ▼
MAINS 2008
Discuss the major extra-constitutional factors influencing the federal polity in India.
✅ Extra-constitutional = factors beyond formal constitutional text. Include: (1) Single party dominance → Centre-State asymmetry (2) Emergency provisions used politically (3) Governor as Centre's agent (4) Finance Commission design → vertical imbalance (5) All-India services = Centre's reach into states. These undermine formal federal design. Sarkaria Commission tried to address many. SR Bommai 1994 corrected one (Art 356 misuse).
PRELIMS 2012
The concept of "Welfare State" finds explicit mention in which part of the Constitution?
(a) Preamble (b) Fundamental Rights (c) DPSP (d) Fundamental Duties
✅ (c) DPSP — Directive Principles of State Policy (Part IV) — Ambedkar called it a "novel feature." DPSPs commit the state to welfare goals: equal pay, free legal aid, just working conditions, living wage, right to work etc. Preamble mentions "Justice (social, economic, political)" but DPSP is the explicit welfare state instrument.
PRELIMS 2013
Which part of the Indian Constitution has been described as the "conscience of the Constitution" by Dr. Ambedkar?
✅ Dr. Ambedkar called Article 32 (Right to Constitutional Remedies) as the "heart and soul of the Constitution" — not conscience. "Conscience" is sometimes attributed to DPSP. The key quote: Art 32 = "heart and soul" because without remedy, rights are meaningless. Always know exact Ambedkar quotes.
MAINS 2014 (GS-II)
Though the federal principle is dominant in our Constitution and is one of its basic features, it is equally true that federalism under Indian Constitution leans in favour of a strong Centre. Discuss. [12.5 Marks]
✅ The prototype federalism Mains question — asked 8+ times in 30 years in different words! Always use: Federal features (5 points) + Unitary features (7 points including Governor, Art 3, emergency provisions, all-India services, single citizenship) + Scholars (Wheare, Austin, Morris Jones, Jennings) + SC cases (SR Bommai 1994, Kesavananda) + Conclude: purposive federalism for unity.
PRELIMS 2015
Other than Fundamental Rights, which parts of the Constitution reflect principles of Universal Declaration of Human Rights (1948)? 1.Preamble 2.DPSP 3.Fundamental Duties
✅ 1, 2 and 3 all — Preamble (justice, liberty, equality = UDHR values), DPSP (social and economic rights mirror UDHR), Fundamental Duties (Art 51-A reflects UDHR obligations). This is a nuanced question. Only incorrect answer would be "Fundamental Rights only."
📙 2016–2020 ▼
MAINS 2016 (GS-II)
Discuss each adjective attached to the word 'Republic' in the Preamble. Are they defendable in present circumstances? [12.5 Marks]
✅ "Sovereign Democratic Republic" (1950 original) + "Socialist" and "Secular" (added 1976). Sovereign: YES — India makes its own foreign policy, though WTO/IMF commitments raise nuanced questions. Socialist: India = democratic socialism (mixed economy) not Marxist socialism. YES, welfare programs like PM-GKY, MGNREGS support. Secular: YES — equal respect per SC, though communalism remains a challenge. Democratic: YES — 17 general elections held. Republic: YES — elected President.
PRELIMS 2017
Consider: 1. The term 'secular' was added to the Preamble by 42nd Amendment 1976. 2. The Preamble secures liberty of belief, faith and worship to all citizens.
✅ Both correct — "Secular" added by 42nd Amendment 1976. The Preamble grants liberty of thought, expression, belief, faith and worship to all citizens. Classic paired-statement Prelims format on Preamble.
MAINS 2019 (GS-II)
What can France learn from the Indian Constitution's approach to secularism? [10 Marks]
✅ France = laïcité (aggressive separation — bans religious symbols in public spaces, e.g., hijab ban). India = positive secularism (tolerates religious expression, state engages religion for reform — Art 25's "subject to public order, morality, health, and other provisions"). France could learn: accommodation of religious diversity rather than exclusion; state engagement for social reform without endorsing religion; protection of minority religious identity without forcing assimilation.
PRELIMS 2020
Which part of the Constitution declares the ideal of Welfare State?
✅ DPSP — Part IV — contains directives for social and economic welfare. Preamble contains "justice" but DPSP is the explicit welfare state machinery. Commonly confused — Preamble mentions "social justice" but DPSP is where the welfare state mandate sits. Minerva Mills 1980: balance between FR and DPSP = bedrock.
📔 2021–2025 — Current Era ▼
PRELIMS 2021
What was India's exact constitutional status on 26 January 1950?
✅ Sovereign Democratic Republic — NOT "Socialist Secular Democratic Republic." "Socialist" and "Secular" were added ONLY by 42nd Amendment 1976. Original Preamble (1950) had only: "Sovereign Democratic Republic." This is a perennial UPSC trap — asked 4+ times in 30 years!
PRELIMS 2022
Consider: 1. The Constitution of India defines its 'basic structure' in terms of federalism, secularism, FRs and democracy. 2. The Constitution provides for 'judicial review' to safeguard citizens' liberties and preserve constitutional ideals.
✅ Statement 1: WRONG — Constitution does NOT define Basic Structure anywhere. It is a JUDICIAL doctrine from Kesavananda Bharati 1973. Statement 2: CORRECT — Art 32 (SC), Art 226 (HC) provide judicial review. Answer: Only Statement 2. The "basic structure is in Constitution" trap appears almost every year!
PRELIMS 2023
In essence, what does "Due Process of Law" mean?
✅ Due Process (USA) = courts examine both substance (is the law fair itself?) AND procedure (is the law applied fairly?). India uses "procedure established by law" (Art 21) = narrower, only procedural examination. This is why India's judicial review of laws is narrower than USA's. Maneka Gandhi 1978 expanded India's Art 21 somewhat toward substantive due process but still not equivalent to USA.
MAINS 2022 (GS-II)
Though the federal principle is dominant in our Constitution and is one of its basic features, it is true that federalism under Indian Constitution leans in favour of a strong Centre. Discuss. [10 Marks]
✅ Same question as 2014 — UPSC recycled it! 2022 = exact same question as 2014. Use same model answer. Federal features: 3 lists, independent SC, bicameralism, written Constitution, rigid amendment. Unitary features: single citizenship, strong centre, emergency converts federal → unitary, Governor appointment, all-India services, Art 3. Conclusion: purposive federalism = right balance for India's diversity.
MAINS 2024 (GS-II) · ASKED THIS YEAR!
Discuss India as a secular state and compare with the secular principles of the US Constitution.
✅ India: POSITIVE secularism — equal respect to all religions; state CAN engage with religion (reform untouchability, regulate religious endowments); no official religion. USA: NEGATIVE secularism — First Amendment Establishment Clause = strict separation (no state endorsement of religion); Free Exercise Clause = individual religious freedom. KEY DIFFERENCE: India allows state to intervene in religion for social reform; USA's "wall of separation" (Jefferson) prohibits this. Balram Singh 2024 = latest SC affirmation of India's secularism. Both protect religious freedom but differently.
MAINS 2025 (GS-II)
The Indian Constitution has conferred amending power on Parliament. Examine the procedural and substantive limitations on Parliament's amending power. (250w)
✅ Procedural: Art 368 — (1) Special majority only (2/3rd + majority of total membership), (2) Special majority + half states ratification, (3) Simple majority (outside Art 368). Substantive: Basic Structure doctrine (Kesavananda 1973) — Parliament cannot alter essential features: federalism, secularism, democracy, independence of judiciary, rule of law, free elections. Balram Singh 2024 = latest affirmation. ONOE Bill 2024 = tests whether simultaneous elections violates federalism (basic structure) — JPC examining.
17 SALIENT FEATURES — Exam-Optimised Cards
01
Lengthiest Written Constitution PRE ⭐
Original: 395 Articles, 22 Parts, 8 Schedules. Now: ~470 Articles, 25 Parts, 12 Schedules. 4 reasons for size: diversity, GOI 1935 influence, single constitution for Centre+States, legal luminaries. Trap: "Socialist/Secular not in original 1950 Preamble" — asked 4+ times!
02
Drawn from Various Sources PRE ⭐⭐⭐
Main: GOI 1935 (>50% provisions). UK→parliamentary govt. USA→FRs, judicial review. Ireland→DPSP. Canada→strong Centre. Australia→Concurrent List. Germany→Emergency suspension of FRs. USSR→FDs. France→liberty-equality-fraternity. S.Africa→amendment. Japan→"procedure established by law."
03
Blend of Rigidity & Flexibility PRE ⭐⭐
Art 368 — Type 1: Special majority. Type 2: Special majority + half states. Type 3 (outside 368): Simple majority. India = neither rigid nor flexible. Classification by Lord James Bryce.
04
Federal System with Unitary Bias MAINS ⭐⭐⭐ · 30 YEARS!
Federal: 2 govts, 3 lists, SC, bicameralism, written constitution.
Unitary: Single constitution, single citizenship, strong Centre, Governor appointed by Centre, all-India services, emergency provisions, Art 3.
Art 1 = "Union of States" NOT "Federation." K.C. Wheare: quasi-federal.
05
Parliamentary Form MAINS ⭐⭐
Westminster Model. Features: nominal + real executive, collective responsibility, PM leadership, dissolution of Lok Sabha, majority party rule. Difference from UK: India's Parliament NOT sovereign; India has elected head (republic) vs UK hereditary (monarchy).
06
Parliamentary Sovereignty + Judicial Supremacy MAINS ⭐⭐⭐
Synthesis: SC can declare laws unconstitutional (judicial review). Parliament can amend most provisions. Basic Structure (1973) = ultimate limit. India's "procedure established by law" (Art 21) = narrower than USA's "due process." Key Prelims Q: due process vs procedure established by law.
07
Integrated & Independent Judiciary
Single hierarchy: SC → HC → District Courts. Unlike USA (separate federal + state judiciaries). Independence: security of tenure, fixed service conditions, expenses on CFI, ban on practice after retirement, power to punish contempt.
08
Fundamental Rights (Part III) MAINS ⭐⭐⭐
6 FRs (7 originally — Right to Property removed 44th Amendment 1978 → Art 300-A). Justiciable. 5 writs (habeas corpus, mandamus, prohibition, certiorari, quo warranto). Suspended during National Emergency EXCEPT Art 20 & 21. Ambedkar: Art 32 = "heart and soul."
09
DPSP (Part IV) PRE ⭐⭐
Ambedkar: "novel feature." 3 types: Socialistic, Gandhian, Liberal-Intellectual. Non-justiciable but "fundamental in governance." Welfare State ideal. Minerva Mills 1980: "bedrock of balance between FR and DPSP."
10
Fundamental Duties (Part IV-A)
Added 42nd Amendment 1976 (Swaran Singh Committee). 86th Amendment 2002 = 11th duty added → 11 FDs total. Art 51-A only. Non-justiciable. 0 FDs in original 1950 Constitution.
11
Secular State MAINS ⭐⭐⭐ · EVERY 2 YRS HOT 2024
"Secular" added to Preamble by 42nd Amendment 1976. India = POSITIVE secularism (equal respect, state can reform) vs Western NEGATIVE (strict separation). SC: SR Bommai 1994 + Balram Singh 2024 = Secularism is basic structure. Art 25-28 = religious freedom.
12
Universal Adult Franchise
All citizens ≥ 18 years. Voting age 21 → 18 by 61st Amendment 1988. No discrimination on caste, race, religion, sex, literacy, wealth. Bold experiment at independence given illiteracy levels.
13
Single Citizenship
Despite federal structure — only Indian citizenship (unlike USA's dual citizenship). All citizens enjoy same rights nationwide. Unitary feature in disguise.
14
Independent Bodies PRE ⭐⭐
Election Commission, CAG (guardian of public purse), UPSC, SPSC. Independence: security of tenure + expenses on Consolidated Fund of India.
15
Emergency Provisions PRE ⭐⭐⭐
3 types: Art 352 (armed rebellion — not "internal disturbance," 44th Amend trap). Art 356/365 (State/President's Rule). Art 360 (Financial — NEVER proclaimed). Federal → Unitary transformation without formal amendment.
16
Three-Tier Government PRE ⭐⭐
Unique — not in any other constitution. 73rd Amendment 1992: Panchayats (Part IX, Sch 11). 74th Amendment 1992: Municipalities (Part IX-A, Sch 12). 3 types of municipalities.
17
Co-operative Societies
97th Amendment 2011: FR to form co-ops (Art 19). Art 43-B DPSP. New Part IX-B (Art 243-ZH to 243-ZT).
📰 Current Affairs 2024–25 — Chapter 4 (Highest CA Density)
DEC 2024 · FEATURE 4+5+15 MAINS ⭐⭐⭐
Constitution (129th Amendment) Bill 2024 — ONOE (One Nation One Election)
Introduced 17 Dec 2024, referred to JPC. Proposes new Art 82A — simultaneous elections to Lok Sabha + State Assemblies. Based on Kovind Committee recommendations. Historical precedent: simultaneous elections 1951–1967.
Feature 4 (Federalism): Critics say violates federal structure — state terms curtailed without state consent. SR Bommai 1994: states have independent constitutional identity.
Feature 5 (Parliamentary Govt): Fixed terms undermine collective responsibility principle.
Feature 15 (Emergency): Art 356 (President's Rule) could disrupt synchronised elections.
23rd Law Commission: ONOE does NOT violate basic structure.
→ Mains 2026: "ONOE and federalism" — prepare both sides; Prelims: Art 82A, Kovind Committee
2024 · FEATURE 11 · MAINS 2024 ASKED!
Balram Singh v. UOI (2024) — Secularism Reaffirmed as Basic Structure
SC dismissed petitions challenging "socialist" and "secular" in Preamble. Key: Secularism = Basic Structure (SR Bommai 1994 reaffirmed). Socialism = welfare state commitment (not Marxist). Constitution is a living document. Political debate: Some called for removing these Emergency-era insertions; SC rejected. India = positive secularism: Equal respect to all religions, state can intervene for social reform (unlike USA/France's negative secularism).
→ Direct Mains 2024 answer. Prelims 2026: "secular added by 42nd Amendment + SC reaffirmed 2024"
2025 · FEATURE 4 MAINS ⭐⭐
Kurian Joseph Committee (TN, 2025) — Federal Reset Recommendations
Recommends: Amend Art 368 for state ratification; restrict Art 3 (unilateral boundary change); move Education to State List; revise GST Council voting. Connects to Sarkaria (1983), Punchhi (2007) — both studied Centre-State relations. Post Mohit Minerals 2022 (SC on GST Council as recommendatory, not binding) — states seeking formal federal reset. Static link: Directly addresses India's "federal with unitary bias" critique — all the unitary features listed in Ch 4 Feature 4 are exactly what this committee wants to reduce.
→ Mains 2024 asked: "Suggest measures to build trust between Centre & States" — THIS is the current answer
2024–25 · FEATURE 7+6 · JUDICIAL INDEPENDENCE
Waqf Amendment Act 2024 — SC Judicial Review in Action
Waqf (Amendment) Act 2024 challenged in SC — violates Art 25-26 (religion), Art 14 (equality), secularism as basic structure? SC issued stay. 2024–25 also saw collegium system debates (Feature 7 — independent judiciary) and NJAC aftermath (SC struck down NJAC 2014 as violating judicial independence as basic structure). Static link: Feature 6 (SC checking Parliament via judicial review) + Feature 7 (independent judiciary) both active. India's synthesis of parliamentary sovereignty + judicial supremacy tested in real-time by Waqf challenge.
→ Mains: "SC's role as guardian of Constitution against Parliament's arbitrary power"
⚠️ Top 7 Exam Traps — 30 Year Analysis

05

Preamble of the Constitution

Source of Authority · Nature of State · Objectives · Date of Adoption

📰
Live CA — Chapter 5 · Preamble
Preamble amendments · Socialist/Secular debates · Objectives Resolution · Balram Singh 2024
Click Update Now to fetch this week's CA.
📊 30-Year Exam Pattern — Chapter 5
2–3
Prelims Qs per year
45%
From Preamble words & their meaning
35%
Preamble as part of Constitution / legal status
20%
42nd Amendment — Socialist, Secular added
⚡ 30-year pattern: Is Preamble part of Constitution? (asked 5+ times — YES after Kesavananda 1973). What words were added by 42nd Amendment? (Socialist, Secular, Integrity). What is NOT in Preamble? (Federal — asked 3+ times). Economic Justice in Preamble + DPSP (perennial). Preamble as "Identity Card" of Constitution (N.A. Palkhivala quote).
THE PREAMBLE TEXT
📜
"WE, THE PEOPLE OF INDIA, having solemnly resolved to constitute India into a SOVEREIGN SOCIALIST SECULAR DEMOCRATIC REPUBLIC and to secure to all its citizens: JUSTICE, social, economic and political; LIBERTY of thought, expression, belief, faith and worship; EQUALITY of status and of opportunity; and to promote among them all FRATERNITY assuring the dignity of the individual and the unity and integrity of the Nation; IN OUR CONSTITUENT ASSEMBLY this twenty-sixth day of November, 1949, do HEREBY ADOPT, ENACT AND GIVE TO OURSELVES THIS CONSTITUTION."
4 KEY COMPONENTS
1. Source of Authority
  • "We, the People of India" — Constitution derives authority from the PEOPLE
  • Doctrine of popular sovereignty
2. Nature of Indian State
  • Sovereign — no external authority; full power
  • Socialist — added 42nd Amend 1976; mixed economy + welfare state
  • Secular — added 42nd Amend 1976; equal respect to all religions
  • Democratic — popular sovereignty; adult franchise
  • Republic — elected head (President); no hereditary rule
3. Objectives
  • Justice — social, economic, political
  • Liberty — thought, expression, belief, faith, worship
  • Equality — status and opportunity
  • Fraternity — dignity of individual + unity & integrity of nation
4. Date of Adoption
  • 26 November 1949 — Constitution adopted
  • Preamble enacted AFTER the entire Constitution was enacted
  • Based on "Objectives Resolution" (Nehru, 13 Dec 1946)
PREAMBLE LEGAL STATUS — Key Cases
CaseYearRuling
Berubari Union Case1960Preamble is NOT part of Constitution; cannot be used to interpret constitutional provisions
Kesavananda Bharati1973Preamble IS part of Constitution; can be amended under Art 368 BUT cannot destroy Basic Structure
LIC of India Case1995Reaffirmed: Preamble is part of Constitution (Kesavananda view upheld)
Balram Singh v. UOI2024SC dismissed challenge to "Socialist" & "Secular" in Preamble — these are part of Basic Structure
⚠️
Top Trap: Preamble cannot be used as a SOURCE OF LEGISLATIVE POWER — it only aids in interpretation. Also, Preamble is NON-JUSTICIABLE — courts cannot enforce it independently. These distinctions are asked almost every cycle.
TERMS IN PREAMBLE — Meaning (High-Yield)
TermAdded/OriginalMeaning for UPSC
SovereignOriginal 1950India has supreme power; not subject to external control. BUT: membership of UN, WTO raises questions of qualified sovereignty
Socialist42nd Amendment 1976 ⚠️Democratic socialism (NOT Marxist). Mixed economy — coexistence of public & private sectors. Welfare state commitment.
Secular42nd Amendment 1976 ⚠️Positive secularism — equal respect to all religions. India has no official state religion. SC: SR Bommai 1994, Balram Singh 2024
DemocraticOriginal 1950Broader sense — not just political but social & economic democracy. Universal adult franchise.
RepublicOriginal 1950Elected head (President, 5-year term). No hereditary rule. Political sovereignty in the people. All public offices open to all citizens.
JusticeOriginal 1950Social (eliminate inequality), Economic (equal opportunity in economic sphere), Political (universal franchise, equal political rights)
LibertyOriginal 19505 liberties: thought, expression, belief, faith, worship. NOT absolute — subject to reasonable restrictions. French Revolution ideal.
EqualityOriginal 1950Equality of STATUS and OPPORTUNITY. Does not mean absolute equality but rule of law, no privilege. Art 14–18.
FraternityOriginal 1950Brotherhood. Ensures: (1) dignity of individual, (2) unity and integrity of nation. Linked to single citizenship.
Integrity42nd Amendment 1976 ⚠️Added along with Socialist and Secular. "Unity and integrity of the nation" — territorial and national integration.
🧠 What was NOT in original 1950 Preamble
S · S · I = Three additions by 42nd Amendment 1976
Socialist · Secular · Integrity — all three added by 42nd Constitutional Amendment Act 1976 during Emergency. Original 1950 Preamble only had: "Sovereign Democratic Republic." Asked 5+ times in 30 years!
PYQs — Chapter 5
📜1990–2005▼
PRELIMS 1991
The Preamble of the Indian Constitution was amended by which Amendment Act?
✅ 42nd Constitutional Amendment Act, 1976 — added "Socialist," "Secular" and changed "Unity of the Nation" to "Unity and Integrity of the Nation."
PRELIMS 1994
Which of the following does not find mention in the Preamble? (a) Justice (b) Liberty (c) Fraternity (d) Federal
✅ (d) Federal — The word "Federal" does NOT appear in the Preamble. Art 1 says "Union of States." This is a classic trap asked 3+ times in 30 years.
MAINS 1998
What is the significance of the Preamble of the Indian Constitution?
✅ Key: "Identity Card of Constitution" (N.A. Palkhivala). Based on Objectives Resolution. Part of Constitution (Kesavananda 1973). Cannot be used as source of legislative power. Guides constitutional interpretation. Modified version of Objectives Resolution (Nehru, 13 Dec 1946).
PRELIMS 2001
'Economic Justice' as one of the objectives of the Indian Constitution is provided in: (a) Preamble and FR (b) Preamble and DPSP (c) FR and DPSP (d) None
✅ (b) Preamble and DPSP — Preamble mentions "justice — social, economic and political." DPSP (Part IV) provides the mechanism for achieving economic justice. Fundamental Rights deal with political rights, not economic justice per se.
📘2006–2020▼
PRELIMS 2010
The ideals of liberty, equality and fraternity enshrined in the Preamble were inspired from: (a) Russian Revolution (b) Irish Constitution (c) French Revolution (d) US Constitution
✅ (c) French Revolution (1789) — Liberté, Égalité, Fraternité. DPSP from Irish Constitution. FRs from US Constitution. Important source distinctions frequently tested.
PRELIMS 2013
'Economic Justice' as one of the objectives of the Constitution has been provided in: (a) Preamble and FR (b) Preamble and DPSP (c) FR and DPSP (d) None
✅ (b) Preamble and DPSP — Same question as 2001, repeated! UPSC recycles this exact question. Preamble = "economic justice" as objective. DPSP = mechanism (Art 39, 43 etc.).
PRELIMS 2015
Consider: 1. The term 'secular' was added to Preamble by 42nd Amendment 1976. 2. Preamble secures liberty of belief, faith and worship to all citizens.
✅ Both correct — "Secular" added by 42nd Amendment 1976. Preamble grants "liberty of thought, expression, belief, faith and worship." Frequently tested pairing.
PRELIMS 2020
The Preamble to the Constitution of India is: (a) Not a part, no legal effect (b) Part but no legal effect independently (c) Part with same legal effect as any other part (d) Not part but guides interpretation
✅ (b) — Part of Constitution (Kesavananda 1973) but cannot be independently enforced. Guides interpretation of other provisions. Asked 3+ times in variants.
MAINS 2016
Discuss each adjective attached to the word 'Republic' in the Preamble. Are they defendable?
✅ Adjectives: Sovereign, Socialist, Secular, Democratic. Each must be defended with current examples. Sovereign (yes — independent foreign policy), Socialist (yes — welfare programs), Secular (yes — SC Balram Singh 2024), Democratic (yes — 17 general elections). Republic: elected President (5-year term), no hereditary privilege.
📔2021–2025▼
PRELIMS 2021
What was India's exact constitutional status on 26 January 1950?
✅ Sovereign Democratic Republic — NOT "Socialist Secular Democratic Republic." "Socialist" and "Secular" added ONLY by 42nd Amendment 1976. Classic trap asked 4+ times!
PRELIMS 2023
Consider: 1. The Preamble to the Constitution of India is a part of the Constitution. 2. The Preamble can be amended under Article 368. 3. Preamble cannot be used to enlarge powers of any authority.
✅ All three correct — (1) Part of Constitution: Kesavananda 1973 YES. (2) Can be amended: 42nd Amendment 1976 proves this — but cannot destroy basic structure. (3) Cannot be source of power: Berubari 1960 + Kesavananda 1973 both held this.
MAINS 2024
Discuss India as a secular state and compare with secular principles of the US Constitution.
✅ India = positive secularism (equal respect, state can intervene for social reform). USA = negative secularism (First Amendment, strict wall of separation — Jefferson). Balram Singh 2024 upheld India's secularism as Basic Structure. Direct Preamble question — "Secular" word in Preamble is the hook.
📰 Current Affairs 2024–25 — Chapter 5 (Preamble)
NOV 2024 · SC JUDGMENT · HIGH MAINS RELEVANCE
Balram Singh v. Union of India (2024) — "Socialist" & "Secular" Upheld as Basic Structure
SC dismissed petitions challenging inclusion of "socialist" and "secular" in Preamble (42nd Amendment 1976). SC held these terms are integral to Basic Structure; Constitution is a "living document." Secularism was implicitly present even before 1976 (St. Xavier's 1974). Socialism = welfare state commitment, not Marxist ideology. Political context: Some ruling alliance members called for removing these Emergency-era insertions. SC rejected this definitively.
→ Mains 2024 asked: "Discuss India as a secular state" — Balram Singh 2024 is THE citation for this answer.
NOV 2024 · 75 YEARS OF CONSTITUTION
Constitution Day 75th Year — Preamble at the Centre
PM led celebrations at Supreme Court on 26 November 2024. Emphasis on Preamble as the "soul of the Constitution." Oath-taking ceremonies using Preamble text held nationwide. Renewed debate on whether "We, the People" democratic values are being upheld in governance. Static link: Preamble declares "We, the People" as the source of authority — popular sovereignty as a component of Preamble.
→ Prelims: Preamble declares source of authority; Mains: Preamble as living document

Union and its Territory

Art 1–4 · Types of States · Admission/Formation · Part XXI Special Provisions

📰
Live CA — Chapter 6 · Union & Territory
New States · UT Status · J&K Reorganisation · Delimitation · Border Issues
Click Update Now to fetch this week's CA.
📊 30-Year Exam Pattern — Chapter 6
1–2
Prelims Qs per year
40%
Types of territories (Art 1)
35%
Formation/Reorganisation of States (Art 2, 3)
25%
Special provisions for specific states
⚡ 30-year pattern: Art 1 — "India, that is Bharat, shall be a Union of States" (NOT Federation). Art 3 — Parliament can form new states, alter boundaries without state consent (unitary bias — asked in context of federalism 5+ times). Types of territories under Art 1. States Reorganisation Act 1956 (linguistic basis). J&K reorganisation 2019 is the current affairs hook for this chapter.
ARTICLE 1 — THREE TYPES OF TERRITORIES
TypeDetails
Territories of the States28 States (after Telangana 2014, J&K bifurcation 2019)
Union Territories8 UTs: Delhi (NCT), Puducherry, J&K, Ladakh, Chandigarh, D&N Haveli & Daman & Diu, Lakshadweep, Andaman & Nicobar Islands
Territories that may be acquiredFuture acquisitions (e.g., Goa acquired 1961, Sikkim merged 1975)
⭐
Key distinction: India = "Union of States" (NOT "Federation of States"). Two reasons: (1) Indian federation is NOT the result of an agreement by the states. (2) No state has the RIGHT to secede from the Union. This is asked almost every Prelims cycle in some form.
FORMATION OF NEW STATES — Article 3
⚠️
Art 3 — Parliament CAN, without state's consent: Form new states (by separation/union/combination), increase/decrease area of states, alter boundaries of states, alter names of states. BUT: Bill must be referred to affected state legislature for its views (not binding). This is the UNITARY feature — asked in context of federalism!
STATES REORGANISATION — Key Timeline
YearEventSignificance
1956States Reorganisation Act — linguistic basisMost significant reorganisation; created 14 States + 6 UTs
1960Bombay bifurcatedMaharashtra + Gujarat
1963Nagaland1st state carved from Assam
1966Punjab trifurcatedPunjab + Haryana + Himachal Pradesh
1971Himachal Pradesh statehoodWas UT before
2000Three new statesChhattisgarh (MP), Uttarakhand (UP), Jharkhand (Bihar)
2014TelanganaCarved from Andhra Pradesh — 29th state
2019J&K Reorganisation ActState → Two UTs: J&K (legislature) + Ladakh (no legislature). 28 States + 8 UTs now.
PYQs — Chapter 6
📜1990–2010▼
PRELIMS 1993
The territory of India includes: (a) Territories of states only (b) UTs only (c) Both states and UTs (d) States, UTs and territories that may be acquired
✅ (d) — Art 1(3): territory of India = (1) territories of the states, (2) UTs specified in First Schedule, (3) such other territories as may be acquired. Three-part definition.
PRELIMS 1998
For creation of a new state, Parliament needs to: (a) Get consent of affected state (b) Only refer the bill to affected state legislature (c) Get approval of President only (d) None of the above
✅ (b) — Art 3: Parliament only needs to REFER the bill to affected state legislature for its views (within a fixed time). Parliament is NOT bound by the state legislature's views. This unilateral power = key unitary feature of Indian federalism.
MAINS 2004
Analyse the basis of reorganisation of states in India after independence.
✅ Key: Initially: administrative convenience (British legacy). 1953 — Andhra created on linguistic basis (after Potti Sriramulu's death). 1956 States Reorganisation Act — linguistic principle adopted. BUT: security (Nagaland), tribal identity (Jharkhand, Chhattisgarh), administrative viability (Uttarakhand) also considered later. Latest: Telangana 2014 = political + developmental factors.
📔2015–2025▼
PRELIMS 2022
Consider: 1. India is described as "Union of States" because it is indestructible. 2. A state can unilaterally alter its own name under Article 3.
✅ Statement 1 CORRECT — "Union of States" = indestructible union; no right to secede. Statement 2 WRONG — alteration of state names requires Parliament's action under Art 3 + state legislature must be consulted (though opinion is not binding). State CANNOT unilaterally alter its name.
PRELIMS 2024
How many Union Territories does India currently have?
✅ 8 Union Territories — After J&K Reorganisation Act 2019: (1) Delhi NCT (2) Puducherry (3) J&K (4) Ladakh (5) Chandigarh (6) D&N Haveli & Daman & Diu (merged 2020) (7) Lakshadweep (8) Andaman & Nicobar Islands. Note: D&N Haveli and Daman & Diu were merged into one UT in 2020.
MAINS 2023
The process of state formation in India has not been consistent. Critically analyse.
✅ Inconsistency: multiple bases used — linguistic (1956), administrative convenience, tribal identity, developmental backwardness, political pressures. J&K 2019 = security/constitutional reasons. Andhra Pradesh demand for re-merger with Telangana in 2024 shows ongoing demands. Issue: no clear criteria; Parliament's Art 3 power = political tool.
📰 Current Affairs 2024–25 — Chapter 6
2024 · J&K STATEHOOD DEMAND
J&K Statehood Restoration Demand — Supreme Court Verdict (2023) + Elections (2024)
SC in October 2023 upheld abrogation of Art 370 and directed elections in J&K by September 2024. J&K Assembly elections held September-October 2024 (National Conference won). Statehood restoration for J&K remains pending — Union Territory status continues. Static link: J&K Reorganisation Act 2019 (Art 3) — Parliament unilaterally bifurcated J&K state into two UTs. This is the most powerful example of Parliament's power under Art 3 being used.
→ Prelims: 8 UTs, J&K as UT with legislature; Mains: Art 3 and federalism
2026 · DELIMITATION
Delimitation Exercise — Constitutional and Political Controversy
Delimitation of constituencies based on 2026 census (or post-2026) remains contentious. Southern states fear loss of Lok Sabha seats due to lower population growth. Critics argue this violates federal balance — states that managed population better will be "penalised." Static link: Art 81 + Fourth Schedule — allocation of seats to states. Delimitation connects to Art 1 (Union of States) and the principle of equal representation.
→ Mains 2026: "Delimitation and federal concerns" — very high probability question
